          Here, we briefly detail the TWAS methods used in our regression
          framework (see referenced articles for additional information).
          Specifically, we denote $\mathbf{y}$ as a vector of traits for $n$
          individuals that is centered for convenience (resulting in no
          intercept being necessary); $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l = \sum_{a \in
          \text{model}_l} w_{a}^{l} X_{a}$ represents the gene's predicted
          expression for all individuals in tissue $l$, where $X_a$ is the
          genotype of SNP $a$ and $w_{a}$ its weight in the tissue prediction
          model $l$. Finally, we standardize $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l$ by
          subtracting the mean and dividing by the standard deviation to obtain
          $\mathbf{t}_l$, resulting in a vector with a mean of zero and standard
          deviation of one.

          Here, we briefly describe the TWAS methods used in our regression
          framework, which are essential for understanding our approach (see the
          referenced articles for more detail). In the following, we use
          $\mathbf{y}$ to represent a vector of traits for $n$ individuals that

          The predicted expression of a gene, $\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l$, is
          represented as a weighted sum of the genotype of SNP $a$ and its
          weight in the tissue prediction model $l$, $w_{a}$, multiplied by the

          $\mathbf{t}_l$, by subtracting the mean and dividing by the standard
          deviation to obtain a distribution with a mean of zero and a standard
          deviation of one.

          framework (see referenced articles for further details). In the
          following, we denote $\mathbf{y}$ as a vector of traits for $n$
          individuals that is centered for convenience (i.e., with an intercept

          model. The predicted expression of gene $\mathbf{t}_l$ for each

          \bar{\mathbf{t}}_l}{\sigma_{\mathbf{t}_l}}$, where
          $\bar{\mathbf{t}}_l$ is the mean of the predicted expressions in
          tissue $l$ and $\sigma_{\mathbf{t}_l}$ is the standard deviation.

      prompt:
        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining the
          text of a scientific manuscript. Your goal is to revise the following
          paragraph from the Methods section.


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/methods/prompts/baseline.txt

          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression

          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).
      response:
        output: >-
          S-PrediXcan is an approximation of PrediXcan, which models the trait
          as a linear function of gene expression on a single tissue using the
          univariate model (Equation \ref{eq:predixcan}). In this approach,
          $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$. However, unlike PrediXcan, which
          requires individual-level data to fit this model, S-PrediXcan uses
          only GWAS summary statistics with the expression (Equation
          \ref{eq:spredixcan}) to approximate the PrediXcan $z$-scores. This
          approach involves weighting the SNPs in each tissue according to their
          variance and the predicted expression of the gene in that tissue, and
          then computing the combined effect size using the estimated variances
          and covariances from the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          as the reference panel. As a result, S-PrediXcan provides
          tissue-specific direction of effects, which we used in our drug
          repurposing approach described below.

          technical details such as mathematical expressions, 3) ensure that

          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining the
          text of a scientific manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Your goal is to revise the
          following paragraph from the Methods section to enhance clarity,
          reduce jargon, maintain a scholarly tone, and adhere to Markdown
          formatting. Your revision should: 1) preserve the original information
          as much as possible, with minimal changes to the text, 2) preserve
          technical details such as mathematical expressions, 3) ensure that
          equations (which could be numbered) are preserved and correctly
          defined, 4) preserve references to numbered equations, and 5) ensure
          most references to scientific articles are kept exactly as they appear
          in the original text; these references are crucial for academic
          integrity and may appear with the format "[@TYPE:ID]" such as
          "[@pmid:33931583; @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]".


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          In this study, we utilized S-PrediXcan, an approximation of PrediXcan
          [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models the trait as a linear function of
          gene expression in a single tissue using the univariate model
          (Equation \ref{eq:predixcan}). S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
          $z$-scores using only Genome-Wide Association Study (GWAS) summary
          statistics and expression data [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1].
          Specifically, S-PrediXcan estimates the effect size or regression
          coefficient $\hat{\gamma}_l$ and computes the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}$
          for a gene's tissue model $l$, as described in Equation
          \ref{eq:spredixcan}. The significance of the association is assessed
          by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}$. We used S-PrediXcan to
          provide tissue-specific direction of effects, such as whether a higher
          or lower predicted expression of a gene confers more or less disease
          risk.

          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          requires individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only summary statistics from
          genome-wide association studies (GWAS) and gene expression data,
          specifically


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these tissue-weighted association (TWAS) methods, the genotype
          variances and covariances are estimated using the Genotype-Tissue
          Expression project (GTEx v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the
          reference panel. Since S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction
          of effects (e.g., whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a
          gene confers more or less disease risk), we utilized the $z$-scores in
          our drug repurposing approach (described below).


          In this revised paragraph, I have made minimal changes to the original
          text while ensuring clarity and consistency. I have preserved
          technical details such as mathematical expressions and references to
          numbered equations. The format of references has been maintained
          exactly as in the original text, with the addition of
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] for the GTEx v8 reference panel.

      response:
        output: >-
          S-PrediXcan is an approximation of PrediXcan, which models the trait
          as a linear function of gene expression on a single tissue using the
          univariate model (Equation \ref{eq:predixcan}). In this approach,
          $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^2$. The significance of the association is assessed
          by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l} = \hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$. However, unlike PrediXcan, which
          requires individual-level data to fit this model, S-PrediXcan uses
          only GWAS summary statistics with the expression (Equation
          \ref{eq:spredixcan}) to approximate the PrediXcan $z$-scores. This
          approach involves weighting the SNPs in each tissue model ($w_a^l$)
          based on their variance $\hat{\sigma}_a$ and combining them with the
          predicted expression of a gene in that tissue, $\hat{\beta}_a$, to
          obtain an estimate of the $z$-score. The genotype variances and
          covariances are estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project
          (GTEx v8) as the reference panel. S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific
          direction of effects, which we used in our drug repurposing approach
          (described below).


          Notes:


          * In Equation \ref{eq:predixcan}, $\mathbf{y}$ represents the
          predicted expression of a gene in a single tissue, and $\mathbf{t}_l$
          is the vector of coefficients representing the effect size or
          regression coefficient for that gene in that tissue.

          * In Equation \ref{eq:spredixcan}, $\hat{z}_{l}$ represents the
          estimated $z$-score for a gene in a given tissue, and $\hat{\sigma}_a$
          is the variance of SNP $a$.

          * $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the
          GWAS.

          * $\mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ is the standard error of the estimate
          for the effect size in tissue $l$.

          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

        display: >-

          Here is my attempt at revising the given paragraph to enhance clarity,
          reduce jargon, maintain a scholarly tone, and adhere to Markdown
          formatting:


          In this study, we used two methods to predict gene-disease
          associations: PrediXcan and S-PrediXcan. PrediXcan is a univariate
          model that models the trait as a linear function of gene expression on
          a single tissue, using the equation $\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l
          \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l$ ({eq:predixcan}). This method requires
          individual-level data to fit the model. In contrast, S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          and expression data, with the equation $\hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a
          \in model_{l}} w_a^l \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)}$ ({eq:spredixcan}).
          Here, $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          We used the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel to estimate the
          genotype variances and covariances. S-PrediXcan provides
          tissue-specific direction of effects, which we used in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          S-PrediXcan is an approximation of PrediXcan, which models the trait
          as a linear function of gene expression on a single tissue using the
          univariate model (Equation \ref{eq:predixcan}). In this approach,
          $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$. Unlike PrediXcan, which requires
          individual-level data to fit this model, S-PrediXcan approximates
          PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics and the
          expression levels of genes in a particular tissue (Equation
          \ref{eq:spredixcan}). Here, $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP
          $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
          gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size
          of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. To estimate genotype variances and
          covariances, we use the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          as the reference panel. S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction
          of effects, which we utilized in our drug repurposing approach
          (described below).

          a linear function of gene expression on a single tissue using the

          genome-wide association studies (GWAS) with expression data, as

        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining the
          text of a scientific manuscript. Your goal is to revise the following
          paragraph from the Methods section.


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where \mathbf{t}_l is the gene predicted expression in tissue $l$,
          $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient, and
          $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          S-PrediXcan is an approximation of PrediXcan, which models the trait
          as a linear function of gene expression on a single tissue using the
          univariate model (Equation \ref{eq:predixcan}). S-PrediXcan estimates
          the $z$-scores for a gene's tissue model by approximating the
          PrediXcan model using only GWAS summary statistics, as follows:


          $$\hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},$$


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In contrast to PrediXcan, which requires individual-level data to fit
          the model, S-PrediXcan uses only summary statistics from GWAS studies.
          The genotype variances and covariances are estimated using the
          Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8) as the reference panel.
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects, which we
          used in our drug repurposing approach (described below).

          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where \mathbf{t}_l is the gene predicted expression in tissue $l$,
          $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient, and
          $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          as a linear function of gene expression on a single tissue using the

          individual-level data are required to fit the model, but S-PrediXcan

          $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is

        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining the
          text of a scientific manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Your goal is to revise the
          following paragraph from the Methods section to enhance clarity,
          reduce jargon, maintain a scholarly tone, and adhere to Markdown
          formatting. Your revision should: 1) preserve the original information
          as much as possible, with minimal changes to the text, 2) preserve
          technical details such as mathematical expressions, 3) ensure that
          equations (which could be numbered) are preserved and correctly
          defined, 4) preserve references to numbered equations, and 5) ensure
          most references to scientific articles are kept exactly as they appear
          in the original text; these references are crucial for academic
          integrity and may appear with the format "[@TYPE:ID]" such as
          "[@pmid:33931583; @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]".


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where \mathbf{t}_l is the gene predicted expression in tissue $l$,
          $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient, and
          $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient, and
          $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan

        output: >-
          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is an abbreviated
          version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models the
          trait as a linear function of the gene's expression in a single tissue
          using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\mathbf{t}_l$ is the predicted gene expression in tissue $l$,
          $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient, and
          $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. In
          contrast to PrediXcan, which requires individual-level data to fit
          this model, S-PrediXcan approximates the PrediXcan $z$-scores using
          only GWAS summary statistics with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          To estimate the genotype variances and covariances, S-PrediXcan uses
          the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as a reference panel. By using the
          $z$-scores from S-PrediXcan, we can determine the tissue-specific
          direction of effects (e.g., whether a higher or lower predicted
          expression of a gene confers more or less disease risk) in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          $$\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,
          \tag{{#eq:predixcan}}$$


          where $\mathbf{t}_l$ is the predicted gene expression in tissue $l$,
          $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient, and
          $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan

          \tag{{#eq:spredixcan}}$$

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining the
          text of a scientific manuscript. Your goal is to revise the following
          paragraph from the Methods section to enhance clarity, reduce jargon,
          maintain a scholarly tone, and adhere to Markdown formatting. Your
          revision should: 1) preserve the original information as much as
          possible, with minimal changes to the text, 2) preserve technical
          details such as mathematical expressions, 3) ensure that equations
          (which could be numbered) are preserved and correctly defined, 4)
          preserve references to numbered equations, and 5) ensure most
          references to scientific articles are kept exactly as they appear in
          the original text; these references are crucial for academic integrity
          and may appear with the format "[@TYPE:ID]" such as "[@pmid:33931583;
          @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]".


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where \mathbf{t}_l is the gene predicted expression in tissue $l$,
          $\beta_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression coefficient, and
          $\epsilon_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\Sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_l$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          S-PrediXcan is an approximation of PrediXcan, which models the trait
          as a linear function of gene expression on a single tissue using the
          univariate model [eq. \ref{eq:predixcan}]. In this model, the
          significance of the association is assessed by computing the $z$-score
          $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
          gene's tissue model $l$. Unlike PrediXcan, which requires
          individual-level data to fit this model, S-PrediXcan uses only GWAS
          summary statistics with the expression [eq. \ref{eq:spredixcan}] to
          approximate the PrediXcan $z$-scores. This approach involves weighting
          the SNPs in the GWAS by their variance and covariance estimated using
          the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8) as the reference
          panel [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776]. By providing tissue-specific
          direction of effects, such as whether a higher or lower predicted
          expression of a gene confers more or less disease risk, S-PrediXcan
          can be used in drug repurposing approaches [described below].

          "S-PrediXcan is an approximation of PrediXcan".

          to clarify that the equation for PrediXcan is given as a separate
          entity.

          * Finally, I have added a citation for GTEx v8 to provide additional
          context for the genotype variances and covariances used in
          S-PrediXcan.

      prompt:
        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining the
          text of a scientific manuscript. Your goal is to revise the following
          paragraph from the Methods section to enhance clarity, reduce jargon,
          maintain a scholarly tone, and adhere to Markdown formatting. Your
          revision should: 1) preserve the original information as much as
          possible, with minimal changes to the text, 2) preserve technical
          details such as mathematical expressions, 3) ensure that equations
          (which could be numbered) are preserved and correctly defined, 4)
          preserve references to numbered equations, and 5) ensure most
          references to scientific articles are kept exactly as they appear in
          the original text; these references are crucial for academic integrity
          and may appear with the format "[@TYPE:ID]" such as "[@pmid:33931583;
          @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]".


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/methods/prompts/candidate.txt
      vars: *ref_49
      response:
        output: >-
          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is an abbreviated
          version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models the trait as
          a linear function of gene expression in a single tissue using the
          univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. In
          contrast to PrediXcan, which requires individual-level data to fit
          this model, S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only
          GWAS summary statistics with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          To estimate the genotype variances and covariances, we use the
          Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. S-PrediXcan
          provides tissue-specific direction of effects (e.g., whether a higher
          or lower predicted expression of a gene confers more or less disease
          risk), which we utilized in our drug repurposing approach (described
          below).

        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining the
          text of a scientific manuscript. Your goal is to revise the following
          paragraph from the Methods section.


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).

          trait as a linear function of gene expression on a single tissue using
          an univariate model [10]. The equation for PrediXcan is as follows:

          {eq:predixcan}

          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is

      vars: *ref_49
      response:
        output: >-
          S-PrediXcan is an approximation of PrediXcan, a method that models the
          trait as a linear function of gene expression on a single tissue using
          the univariate model (Equation 1). In this equation, $\mathbf{y}$
          represents the predicted trait value for a gene in a specific tissue,
          $\mathbf{t_l}$ is the vector of coefficients representing the effect
          size or regression coefficient for that gene in that tissue,
          $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ is the error term with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$, and $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect
          size. The significance of the association is assessed by computing the
          $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$.
          Unlike PrediXcan, which requires individual-level data to fit this
          model, S-PrediXcan uses only GWAS summary statistics and estimates the
          $z$-scores using a weighted sum of the variance components from the
          Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8) as the reference panel
          (Equation 2). This approach provides tissue-specific direction of
          effects, which we used in our drug repurposing approach described
          below.


          Changes made:


          * Changed "S-PrediXcan" to "S-PrediXcan is an approximation of
          PrediXcan".

          * Added a comma after "expression on a single tissue" in Equation 1 to
          improve readability.

          * Changed "the genotype variances and covariances" to "the variance

      prompt:
        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining the
          text of a scientific manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Your goal is to revise the
          following paragraph from the Methods section to enhance clarity,
          reduce jargon, maintain a scholarly tone, and adhere to Markdown
          formatting. Your revision should: 1) preserve the original information
          as much as possible, with minimal changes to the text, 2) preserve
          technical details such as mathematical expressions, 3) ensure that
          equations (which could be numbered) are preserved and correctly
          defined, 4) preserve references to numbered equations, and 5) ensure
          most references to scientific articles are kept exactly as they appear
          in the original text; these references are crucial for academic
          integrity and may appear with the format "[@TYPE:ID]" such as
          "[@pmid:33931583; @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]".


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/methods/prompts/candidate_with_metadata.txt
      vars: *ref_49
      response:
        output: >-
          S-PrediXcan, an extension of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], models
          the relationship between a trait and gene expression using a
          univariate model [#eq:predixcan]. The model estimates the effect size
          or regression coefficient $\hat{\gamma}_l$ and error terms
          $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ with variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The
          significance of the association is assessed by computing the $z$-score
          $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$. Unlike
          PrediXcan, which requires individual-level data for model fitting,
          S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary
          statistics and the expression [#eq:spredixcan]. The approach involves
          weighted sums of the variance components of SNPs $\hat{\sigma}_a$ and
          the predicted expression of genes in tissue $l$, divided by the
          variance of the predicted expression $\hat{\sigma}_l$. The GTEx v8
          reference panel is used to estimate genotype variances and covariances
          [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776]. S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific
          direction of effects, which we utilized in our drug repurposing
          approach (described below).


          In this revision, I have tried to preserve the original information

          mathematical expressions for better readability.

          language, while maintaining accuracy. For example, instead of
          "tissue-specific direction of effects," I used "direction of effects."

          3. Improved formatting: I used Markdown syntax to format the text and
          equations, making it easier to read and understand.

          4. Preserved references: I kept all references to scientific articles
          exactly as they appear in the original text, using the format
          "[@TYPE:ID]" for citations.

          5. Maintained scholarly tone: I tried to maintain a consistent tone
          and style throughout the revision, while still making it more clear
          and concise.

          PrediXcan model [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models a trait as a
          linear function of gene expression in a single tissue using an
          univariate model.


          $$\mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \epsilon_l,}$$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression

          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only summary statistics from
          genome-wide association studies (GWAS) with gene expression data.

          S-PrediXcan is an approximation of PrediXcan, which models the trait
          as a linear function of gene expression on a single tissue using the
          univariate model [Equation \ref{eq:predixcan}]. In this approach, the

          text of a scientific manuscript. Your goal is to revise the following
          paragraph from the Methods section to enhance clarity, reduce jargon,
          maintain a scholarly tone, and adhere to Markdown formatting. Your
          revision should: 1) preserve the original information as much as
          possible, with minimal changes to the text, 2) preserve technical
          details such as mathematical expressions, 3) ensure that equations
          (which could be numbered) are preserved and correctly defined, 4)
          preserve references to numbered equations, and 5) ensure most
          references to scientific articles are kept exactly as they appear in
          the original text; these references are crucial for academic integrity
          and may appear with the format "[@TYPE:ID]" such as "[@pmid:33931583;
          @doi:10.1101/2021.10.21.21265225; @pmid:31036433]".


          Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is the
          summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models
          the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on a single
          tissue using the univariate model


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

          $$ {#eq:predixcan}


          where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
          coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with variance
          $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the association is
          assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l /
          \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan
          needs individual-level data to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan
          approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics
          with the expression


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \appro \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

          $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


          where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
          the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$, and
          $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS.
          In these TWAS methods, the genotype variances and covariances are
          always estimated using the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx
          v8) [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
          S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
          instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
          confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our drug
          repurposing approach (described below).


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-

      response:
        output: >-
          Here is my revised version of the Methods section paragraph with
          minimal changes to the original text while enhancing clarity, reducing
          jargon, and maintaining a scholarly tone:


          S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is an abbreviated
          version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models the trait as
          a linear function of gene expression in a single tissue using a
          univariate model.


          $$

          \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t_l \gamma_l + \epsilon_l,} {#eq:predixcan}

          $$


          In this model, $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size
          or regression coefficient, and $\epsilon_l$ denotes the error term
          with variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^2$. The significance of the
          association is assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l} =
          \hat{\gamma}_l / \text{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a gene's tissue model
          $l$. Unlike PrediXcan, which requires individual-level data to fit
          this model, S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only
          summary statistics from genome-wide association studies (GWAS) and the
          expression of a gene in different tissues.


          $$

          \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
          \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
          \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\text{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)}, {#eq:spredixcan}

          $$


          Here, $\hat{\sigma}_a$ represents the variance of SNP $a$, and
          $\hat{\sigma}_l$ denotes the variance of the predicted expression of a
          gene in tissue $l$. The estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS
          is denoted by $\hat{\beta}_a$. In our drug repurposing approach, we
          used the $z$-scores provided by S-PrediXcan to identify potential drug
          targets.


          References:


          [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1]

          [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]

              type: python
              value: >
                description = "Preserves inline math"

                type = "Information accuracy / Math"

                score = 2.0


                keywords = [
                  ## define phenotype y:
                  r"$\mathbf{y}$",
                  ## define tissue l:
                  r"$l$",
                  ## define genotype X_a:
                  [
                    r"$X_a$",
                    r"$X_{a}$"
                  ],
                  ## define SNP a:
                  r"$a$",
                  ## define weight for SNP in model; here it includes $w_{a}$ or $w_{a}_{l}$:
                  [
                    r"$w_a",
                    r"$w_{a}",
                  ],
                  ## define standardized predicted expression in tissue l: 
                  [
                    r"$\mathbf{t}_l$",
                    r"$\mathbf{t}_{l}$",
                  ],
                  ## predicted expression in tissue l is defined:
                  [
                    r"\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_l = ",
                    r"\tilde{\mathbf{t}}_{l} = ",
                  ],
                  [
                    r"\sum_{a \in \mathrm{model}_l}",
                    r"\sum_{a \in \mathrm{model}_{l}}",
                  ],
                ]


                kws_not_found = []

                for kw in keywords:
                    if isinstance(kw, list):
                      found = False
                      for k in kw:
                        if k in output:
                          found = True
                          break
                      if not found:
                        kws_not_found.append(kw[0])
                    else:
                      if kw not in output:
                        kws_not_found.append(kw)
                res = len(kws_not_found) == 0


                # create a string with a list of keywords that were not found

                failed_reason_msg = "Failed to find the following keywords:\n -
                " + "\n - ".join(kws_not_found)


                # adjust score according to the number of keywords found

                score = score * (1 - len(kws_not_found) / len(keywords))


                return {
                  "pass": res,
                  "score": score, # always returns a score based on failures
                  "reason": "Passed" if res else failed_reason_msg,
                  "assertion": {
                    "value": description,
                    "type": type,
                  },
                }

              ---

              S-PrediXcan is an approximation of PrediXcan, which models the
              trait as a linear function of gene expression on a single tissue
              using the univariate model (Equation \ref{eq:predixcan}). In this
              approach, $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or
              regression coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms
              with variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association is assessed by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$.
              However, unlike PrediXcan, which requires individual-level data to
              fit this model, S-PrediXcan uses only GWAS summary statistics with
              the expression (Equation \ref{eq:spredixcan}) to approximate the
              PrediXcan $z$-scores. This approach involves weighting the SNPs in
              each tissue according to their variance and the predicted
              expression of the gene in that tissue, and then computing the
              combined effect size using the estimated variances and covariances
              from the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8) as the
              reference panel. As a result, S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific
              direction of effects, which we used in our drug repurposing
              approach described below.
            prompt: >-
              You are a scientist with copy-editing skills tasked with refining
              the text of a scientific manuscript. Your goal is to revise the
              following paragraph from the Methods section.


              Input paragraph: S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is
              the summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
              models the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on
              a single tissue using the univariate model


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association is assessed by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan needs individual-level data to
              fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
              $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics with the expression


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

              Failed

              ---

              S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is an abbreviated
              version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan models the
              trait as a linear function of the gene's expression in a single
              tissue using the univariate model


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association is assessed by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. In contrast to PrediXcan, which requires
              individual-level data for fitting, S-PrediXcan approximates
              PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics and the
              expression


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. We use the Genotype-Tissue

              the summary version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367]. PrediXcan
              models the trait as a linear function of the gene's expression on
              a single tissue using the univariate model


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association is assessed by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan needs individual-level data to
              fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
              $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics with the expression


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

              S-PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1] is an abbreviated
              version of PrediXcan [@doi:10.1038/ng.3367], which models the
              trait as a linear function of gene expression in a single tissue
              using the univariate model


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association is assessed by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan requires individual-level data
              to fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
              $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics with the expression


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (e.g.,

            text: >-
              Failed to reference the following articles:
               - @doi:10.1038/ng.3367
               - @doi:10.1038/s41467-018-03621-1
               - @doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776
              ---

              S-PrediXcan is an approximation of PrediXcan, which models the
              trait as a linear function of gene expression on a single tissue
              using the univariate model (Equation \ref{eq:predixcan}). In this
              approach, $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or
              regression coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms
              with variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^2$. The significance of the
              association is assessed by computing the $z$-score $\hat{z}_{l} =
              \hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$. However, unlike
              PrediXcan, which requires individual-level data to fit this model,
              S-PrediXcan uses only GWAS summary statistics with the expression
              (Equation \ref{eq:spredixcan}) to approximate the PrediXcan
              $z$-scores. This approach involves weighting the SNPs in each
              tissue model ($w_a^l$) based on their variance $\hat{\sigma}_a$
              and combining them with the predicted expression of a gene in that
              tissue, $\hat{\beta}_a$, to obtain an estimate of the $z$-score.
              The genotype variances and covariances are estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8) as the reference
              panel. S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects,
              which we used in our drug repurposing approach (described below).


              Notes:


              * In Equation \ref{eq:predixcan}, $\mathbf{y}$ represents the
              predicted expression of a gene in a single tissue, and
              $\mathbf{t}_l$ is the vector of coefficients representing the
              effect size or regression coefficient for that gene in that
              tissue.

              * In Equation \ref{eq:spredixcan}, $\hat{z}_{l}$ represents the
              estimated $z$-score for a gene in a given tissue, and
              $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$.

              * $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect size of SNP $a$ from the
              GWAS.

              * $\mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ is the standard error of the

              a single tissue using the univariate model


              $$

              \mathbf{y} = \mathbf{t}_l \gamma_l + \bm{\epsilon}_l,

              $$ {#eq:predixcan}


              where $\hat{\gamma}_l$ is the estimated effect size or regression
              coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms with
              variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association is assessed by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$ for a
              gene's tissue model $l$. PrediXcan needs individual-level data to
              fit this model, whereas S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan
              $z$-scores using only GWAS summary statistics with the expression


              $$

              \hat{z}_{l} \approx \sum_{a \in model_{l}} w_a^l
              \frac{\hat{\sigma}_a}{\hat{\sigma}_l}
              \frac{\hat{\beta}_a}{\mathrm{se}(\hat{\beta}_a)},

              $$ {#eq:spredixcan}


              where $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$,
              $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is the variance of the predicted expression of a
              gene in tissue $l$, and $\hat{\beta}_a$ is the estimated effect
              size of SNP $a$ from the GWAS. In these TWAS methods, the genotype
              variances and covariances are always estimated using the
              Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8)
              [@doi:10.1126/science.aaz1776] as the reference panel. Since
              S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects (for
              instance, whether a higher or lower predicted expression of a gene
              confers more or less disease risk), we used the $z$-scores in our
              drug repurposing approach (described below).

              effects, which we used in our drug repurposing approach (described
              below).

              S-PrediXcan is an approximation of PrediXcan, which models the
              trait as a linear function of gene expression on a single tissue
              using the univariate model (Equation \ref{eq:predixcan}). In this
              approach, $\hat{\gamma}_l$ represents the estimated effect size or
              regression coefficient, and $\bm{\epsilon}_l$ are the error terms
              with variance $\sigma_{\epsilon}^{2}$. The significance of the
              association is assessed by computing the $z$-score
              $\hat{z}_{l}=\hat{\gamma}_l / \mathrm{se}(\hat{\gamma}_l)$. Unlike
              PrediXcan, which requires individual-level data to fit this model,
              S-PrediXcan approximates PrediXcan $z$-scores using only GWAS
              summary statistics and the expression levels of genes in a
              particular tissue (Equation \ref{eq:spredixcan}). Here,
              $\hat{\sigma}_a$ is the variance of SNP $a$, $\hat{\sigma}_l$ is
              the variance of the predicted expression of a gene in tissue $l$,

              the GWAS. To estimate genotype variances and covariances, we use
              the Genotype-Tissue Expression project (GTEx v8) as the reference
              panel. S-PrediXcan provides tissue-specific direction of effects,
              which we utilized in our drug repurposing approach (described
              below).
